They attach to an AI Agent's `ai:memory` slot (a dashed sub-connection, PB-T1) and give it a **rolling conversation memory**; the Agent itself consumes them in **PB-T5**. A provider is **never executed as a data step** (the PB-T1 executor skips `role:'provider'` nodes) ‚Äî its params ARE its contract: the consumer resolves them into a `ChatMemoryConfig` and drives the shared chat-memory runtime. **Shared (I5):** NEW `chat-memory.ts` runtime ‚Äî `ChatMemoryConfig` (discriminated `kv`|`postgres`), `loadChatHistory()` (replay the rolling last-N turns before a model turn) + `appendChatTurn()` (persist the new user+assistant pair after), operating ONLY through the injected `ctx.kv`/`ctx.db` capabilities (I3/I6 ‚Äî no driver import, no decrypted secret); `kvMemoryKey()`, `quotePgIdent()` (validates `/^[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*$/` per dot-segment then double-quotes; a hostile table throws), `toAiMessages()`. SQL values ALWAYS bound (`$1,$2,‚Ä¶`), never concatenated; reads `SELECT ‚Ä¶ ORDER BY id DESC LIMIT window*2` then re-orders oldest-first; writes a turn as two bound rows in one `INSERT`. Plus `AiMemoryKvParamsSchema` (`session_key`, `memory_window` default 10) + `AiMemoryPostgresParamsSchema` (`credentialId` `postgres`, `table` default `ctb_chat_memory` validated as a SQL identifier, `session_key`, `memory_window`, `auto_create` ‚Üí `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`) in `node-params.ts`; both exported from the shared index. **Nodes:** `ai/memory-kv.ts` + `ai/memory-postgres.ts` (both `role:'provider'`, `provides:'ai:memory'`, `ports {inputs:[], outputs:['provider']}`, `execute()` fails loud if ever run) + registered in `index.ts`. **Editor:** fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced) ‚Äî `nodes.ai.memoryKv.label`/`nodes.ai.memoryPostgres.label` + `nodeDesc.ai.memory{Kv,Postgres}` + the full `param.ai.memory{Kv,Postgres}.*` / `paramDesc.*` families; the `credentialRef` widget already filters `ai.memoryPostgres` to `postgres` credentials (no widget change). Same `ctx.db` capability contract; the `mysql2` driver + POOL live ONLY in `apps/server` (I3 ‚Äî `core`/`nodes` never import a DB driver). Connection comes from a NEW `mysql` credential (host/port[default 3306]/database/user/password/ssl, AES-256-GCM at rest ‚Äî I7; node sees only a `credentialId`). **Same operations** as db.postgres (`query`/`select`/`insert`/`update`/`delete`, `return_mode`, `confirm_many`, `save_as`) with the **MySQL dialect:** placeholders are positional `?` (not `$1,$2,‚Ä¶`); identifiers are backtick-quoted (`` `col` ``, not `"col"`); there is **NO `RETURNING *`** ‚Äî a write returns the driver's OK packet which the host normalizes to a synthetic row `{affectedRows, insertId?}` so `rows`/`single` still behave. Values ALWAYS bound, identifiers validated against `/^[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*$/`. Runs ONCE per node run; fails LOUDLY when `ctx.db` is null. **Shared (I5):** `MysqlSchema` added to `CredentialDataSchema` discriminatedUnion (+`'mysql'` enum/labels/hint/authHeaders kept exhaustive); `DbQueryRequest` gained `dialect?: 'postgres'|'mysql'` (defaults `postgres` ‚Üí PB-T2 node unchanged); `DbMysqlParamsSchema`/`DbMysqlParams` (mirror of DbPostgres, `credentialType:'mysql'`) reusing `DbOperationSchema`/`DbWhereRowSchema`/`DbValueRowSchema`. **Nodes:** `packages/nodes/src/db/mysql.ts` (backtick `quoteIdent`, `?` placeholders, no RETURNING, sends `dialect:'mysql'`) + registered in `index.ts`. **Server (`wire.ts`):** `makeDb()` made dialect-aware (4-arg: db, key, pgFactory, mysqlFactory) ‚Äî `resolvePool(credentialId, dialect)` validates `data.type !== dialect` (throws "is not a {MySQL|Postgres} credential") and routes to the right factory, cached per credentialId; `mysqlPoolFactory` lazily `createRequire(import.meta.url)`-loads `mysql2` (ESM ‚Äî bare require absent), wraps the callback pool via `.promise()`, and normalizes a write OK packet ‚Üí `{affectedRows, insertId?}` row; INJECTABLE via `WireOptions.mysqlPoolFactory` so tests supply a fake. rules fire ONLY when an OPTIONAL 3rd `nodeMeta` arg is passed ‚Üí Phase-A flows unaffected. **Server:** `node-types.ts` conditionally emits role/inputSlots/provides (OMITTED for plain data nodes ‚Üí byte-identical payload); Prior task (PA-T7) `data.dateTime` ‚Äî Date & Time (parse / format / add-subtract / diff) with IANA timezones AND the Jalali (Persian) calendar ‚Äî DONE. Mirrors n8n's "Date & Time" node, adding first-class Persian-calendar output (`€±€¥€∞€¥/€∞€≥/€≤€¥` with Persian digits) since our users are Iranian. PURE: the only clock is the injected `ctx.now()`; the Gregorian‚ÜîJalali conversion is a hand-written **dependency-free** algorithm (`packages/nodes/src/lib/jalali.ts`, Borkowski method) ‚Äî verified against the platform `Intl` Persian calendar over 1,836 dates (2000‚Äì2050) with ZERO mismatches before trusting it (chosen over a runtime dep per CLAUDE.md). Runs **per item**, merging the result under `save_as` (default `datetime`) onto a CLONE (never mutated; seeds one empty item if input empty). Operations: **`format`**‚Üí`{formatted,iso,epoch}` (timezone-adjusted wall-clock rendered in the chosen calendar via token pattern `YYYY/MM/DD/HH/mm/ss`+`MMMM` month-name, `digits:'persian'` maps `0-9`‚Üí`€∞-€π`); **`add`**‚Üí`{iso,epoch}` (shift by `amount`¬∑`unit`, negative subtracts; years/months use UTC calendar math, smaller units exact millis); **`diff`**‚Üí`{diff,unit}` (`source ‚àí to_value` in `diff_unit`, may be fractional). Wall-clock extracted via `Intl.DateTimeFormat(..).formatToParts` in the chosen IANA `timezone` (empty=UTC) ‚Äî so `2026-06-11T22:00Z` in `Asia/Tehran` correctly rolls to the NEXT Jalali day `1405/03/22`. Lenient `parseDate` accepts epoch-millis / ISO-8601 / `YYYY-MM-DD` / `YYYY/MM/DD`; `source:'value'` runs the raw string through `ctx.eval` first so `{{ }}` resolves. Shared (I5): `DataDateTimeParamsSchema` with a `superRefine` requiring `value` when source=value, `amount` when op=add, `to_value` when op=diff, identifier-only `save_as`, `amount` is `z.coerce.number()`. Node `packages/nodes/src/data/date-time.ts` (registered, palette order after `removeDuplicates`). Editor: auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced; `nodes.data.dateTime.label` + `nodeDesc.data.dateTime` + all `paramDesc.data.dateTime.*` + `option.dateTime.{operation,source,calendar,digits,unit}.*`). PLAN2's `€±€¥€∞€¥/€∞€≥/€≤€¥` + Nowruz `1403/01/01` + round-trip G‚ÜíJ‚ÜíG + leap-year + 12 month-names; parseDate epoch/ISO/slash/junk; format Gregorian-default/Jalali/Persian-month+digits/time-tokens-in-tz/tz-rolls-Jalali-day/custom-save_as/empty-input-runs-once; add days/neg-hours/calendar-months/coerced-string-amount; diff days-from-now/fractional-hours; expressions {{ }}-via-ctx.eval + errors unparseable-date/invalid-tz/schema-rejects-missing-value¬∑amount¬∑to_value/non-identifier-save_as). **verify GREEN** (shared 8f / sandbox 6f / nodes 22f¬∑369 / core 1f / server 35f¬∑279 / editor 14f¬∑135).
Task-prevA3: PA-T6 `data.sort` + `data.limit` + `data.removeDuplicates` ‚Äî small, pure, high-value item-list ops ‚Äî DONE. **`data.sort`** orders items by ‚â•1 dotted keys (stable, multi-key: first row primary, later rows break ties); numeric values (incl. numeric strings) compare numerically, else locale-aware string compare; missing/null/'' values always sort LAST regardless of asc/desc (applied AFTER direction so `desc` can't flip it); input array never mutated (output is a `.slice()`-then-sort). **`data.limit`** keeps the first N (default) or last N items on `main`; `max_items` (z.coerce int ‚â•0, default 10; `0`=no limit; ‚â•length passes through) + `keep` (first|last); items never mutated (same refs in original relative order). **`data.removeDuplicates`** drops repeats keeping the FIRST occurrence (n8n keeps first), order of survivors preserved; `compare` modes: `all_fields` (whole `$json` deep-equal via a key-sorted stable JSON serialization so key order is irrelevant) or `selected_fields` (combined value at chosen dotted `fields` is the dedupe key; missing field encoded as a distinct sentinel so it never collides with literal `null`); fails LOUDLY when `selected_fields` has no `fields`. Shared (I5): `SortFieldRowSchema` (field min-1 + order asc|desc default asc) + `DataSortParamsSchema` (fields min-1); `DataLimitParamsSchema` (max_items z.coerce.int.min(0).default(10) + keep first|last default first); `DataRemoveDuplicatesParamsSchema` (compare all_fields|selected_fields default all_fields + fields string[] optional) + types. Nodes: `packages/nodes/src/data/sort.ts` + `limit.ts` + `remove-duplicates.ts`. Editor: all three auto-surface in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced; `nodes.data.{sort,limit,removeDuplicates}.label` + `nodeDesc.*` + `paramDesc.data.sort.fields` + `option.sort.order.{asc,desc}` + `paramDesc.data.limit.{max_items,keep}` + `option.limit.keep.{first,last}` + `paramDesc.data.removeDuplicates.{compare,fields}` + `option.removeDuplicates.compare.{all_fields,selected_fields}`). NODES.md ¬ßSort + ¬ßLimit + ¬ßRemove Duplicates added. Registry **41** types (was 38; PA-T6 adds 3 ‚Üí 41). **Tests (+27):** `data-sort-limit-dedupe.test.ts` (registry-41 + 3√ómain‚Üímain ports; sort: numeric-asc/numeric-string/desc/multi-key-tiebreak/locale-string/missing-last-both-dirs/stable/no-mutate/empty/reject-empty-fields; limit: first/last/0-no-limit/‚â•length/coerce-string/empty/reject-negative; removeDuplicates: all-fields-dedupe/key-order-irrelevant/selected-fields/multi-field-key/missing‚âÝnull/order-preserved/empty/fail-no-fields). All 9 registry-count guards bumped 38‚Üí41.
Task-prevA2: PA-T5 `data.splitOut` + `data.aggregate` ‚Äî the n8n "Split Out" + "Aggregate" inverse pair ‚Äî DONE. `data.splitOut` splits one item that contains an array field into one item per element (n8n Split Out): ports `main` (one item per element) + `empty` (original when array empty/missing); `include` param: `all_fields` (default, replaces array field with element) or `selected_field_only` (only the element, objects pass through, primitives wrapped in `{value}`); non-array value treated as single-element array (n8n-compatible); items never mutated. `data.aggregate` merges many items into one: `aggregate_all_items` mode wraps every item's $json into an array under `dest_field`; `aggregate_individual_fields` mode collects each named `field` across items into an array under `dest` (defaults to same as `field`), first item's other fields carried through. Both handle empty input gracefully (empty array in output). Shared (I5): `DataSplitOutParamsSchema` (field min-1, include all_fields|selected_field_only default all_fields) + `DataAggregateParamsSchema` (mode + fields[] with AggregateFieldRowSchema + dest_field default 'data') + types. Nodes: `packages/nodes/src/data/split-out.ts` + `packages/nodes/src/data/aggregate.ts`. Editor: both auto-surface in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced; `nodes.data.splitOut.label`/`nodes.data.aggregate.label` + `nodeDesc.*` + `paramDesc.data.splitOut.{field,include}` + `paramDesc.data.aggregate.{mode,fields,dest_field}` + `option.splitOut.include.{all_fields,selected_field_only}` + `option.aggregate.mode.{aggregate_individual_fields,aggregate_all_items}`). NODES.md ¬ßSplit Out + ¬ßAggregate added. Registry **38** types (was 35 before this session; PA-T4 added `data.filter` ‚Üí 36, PA-T5 adds 2 ‚Üí 38).
Task-prevA: PA-T4 `data.filter` ‚Äî DONE. Passes each item through `kept` port if its conditions hold, or `discarded` port otherwise. Reuses the `flow.if` condition engine exactly (compareValues ‚Äî same operators, AND/OR combine) so a user who knows IF already knows Filter. Both ports always emitted (possibly empty). Shared (I5): `DataFilterParamsSchema` (conditions min-1 + combine and|or default and). Node `packages/nodes/src/data/filter.ts`. Editor: fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced). NODES.md ¬ßFilter added. Task-prev5: PA-T3 `data.editFields` ‚Äî the n8n "Edit Fields / Set" power node ‚Äî DONE. A richer sibling of the existing `data.setFields` (kept untouched for backward-compat ‚Äî this is a NEW node, not a relabel), labelled **"Edit Fields (Set)"** in the palette so n8n users find it. Same immutable per-item model (input items never mutated; `$vars` rows apply once per run; empty input still emits one shaped item) plus three powers per row over the basic Set node: (1) **op `rename`** ‚Äî move a value from one dotted path (`name`) to another (`value` = destination path), deleting the source; works in `keep_only_set` mode too (source read from the original item); (2) **`value_mode:'json'`** ‚Äî a STRING `value` is `JSON.parse`d into a real value/array/object (a non-string passes through unchanged); (3) **`enabled`** (default true) ‚Äî a disabled row stays in config but is skipped. Dotted names build nested objects; `keep_only_set` makes the output `$json` start empty. Fails LOUDLY (validated UP FRONT in a `planRow` pass before any item is touched) on a `value_mode:'json'` value that isn't valid JSON, or a `rename` with an empty destination. Shared (I5): `EditFieldRowSchema` (name min-1 ¬∑ value? ¬∑ target json|vars ¬∑ op set|remove|rename ¬∑ value_mode value|json ¬∑ enabled, all defaulted) + `DataEditFieldsParamsSchema` (fields min-1 + keep_only_set) + types. Node `packages/nodes/src/data/edit-fields.ts` (pure helpers `planRow`/`getPath`/`setPath`/`removePath`, immutable structuredClone). Editor: node auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced; namespaced `paramDesc.data.editFields.{fields,value_mode,enabled,keep_only_set}` + `option.op.rename` + `option.editFields.value_mode.{value,json}`). NODES.md ¬ßEdit Fields (Set) added. Registry **35** types. **Tests (+14):** nodes `data-edit-fields.test.ts` (registry-35; set dotted+immutable / json-mode array+object / json-mode non-string passthrough; remove dotted; rename json + rename keep_only_set + rename vars; keep_only_set drops rest; disabled-row skipped; vars once-per-run; empty-input seed; failures empty-fields / blank-name / bad-json-value / empty-rename-dest); registry-count tests bumped 34‚Üí35 (6 files). **verify GREEN:** typecheck clean (6 pkgs) + shared 63 / sandbox 49 / nodes 18(281) / core 16 / server 35(279) / editor 14(135); editor vite build OK.
Task-prevA: PA-T2 `tg.getFile` ‚Äî Telegram media RECEIVE (download + store) ‚Äî DONE. The symmetric sibling of PA-T1 (`tg.sendMedia` SEND): given a Telegram `file_id` (captured by the trigger from a photo/voice/document/video the user sent), DOWNLOAD the bytes and OPTIONALLY STORE them (reusing the P3.5 `SqliteFileStore`) so downstream nodes (`tg.sendMedia` `source:file`, future `ai.speechToText`) can reuse them. This is the "Get a file" left-half of the AI-voice screenshot needed for Phase B. The node never touches the token, the network, or disk (I3/I6): it asks a NEW nullable `ctx.tg.getFile(file_id)` host capability for the bytes (host calls the Bot-API `getFile` via the rate-limited sender ‚Üí `file_path`, then `fetch`-downloads from `https://api.telegram.org/file/bot<token>/<file_path>`, token held host-side in `BotHandle.token`), and ‚Äî when `store` is on ‚Äî hands them to a NEW `ctx.files.write(bytes, mime)` capability (host `putLocal` stamps the run's bot). `file_id` defaults to a `$json` lookup (`$json.file_id` then nested `reply`/`photo`/`voice`/`document`/`audio`/`video` `.file_id`) so it drops in right after a media trigger with no config; explicit param wins. Runs ONCE per node run (one download); result `{file_id, path, url, mime, size, stored_file_id?}` merges under `save_as` (default `file`) onto every item. Fails LOUDLY when `ctx.tg.getFile` absent, when `store:true` but no `ctx.files`, when no `file_id` resolvable, or on a download/transport error. Shared (I5): `TgGetFileParamsSchema` (file_id default '' ¬∑ store default true ¬∑ save_as identifier-regex default 'file', `.strict()`) + `TgGetFileParams`; `TgStoredFile` type; `ctx.tg.getFile?(fileId)‚Üí{bytes,filePath,size,mime}`; `ctx.files` extended with `write(bytes,mime)‚ÜíTgStoredFile`. Core: `ExecutorServices.files` changed to a **per-bot factory** `(botId)=>{read,write}` (DL #15 ‚Äî `write` stamps the run's bot; `read` ignores it, ids globally unique); `buildCtx` calls `services.files(exec.botId)`. Server: `BotHandle.token` added (`gateway.ts`); `wire.ts` `makeFiles(fileStore, botId)` gains `write`‚Üí`putLocal`, `services.files: (botId)=>makeFiles(...)`, and `ctx.tg.getFile` (sender `getFile` call ‚Üí `fetch` download, injectable `fetchImpl`). Editor: node auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced; namespaced `paramDesc.tg.getFile.{file_id,store,save_as}` + `nodes.tg.getFile.label` + `nodeDesc.tg.getFile`). NODES.md ¬ßGet a File added. Registry **34** types. **Tests (+12):** nodes `tg-get-file.test.ts` (resolve from explicit param + `$json.file_id` + nested `voice.file_id` + param-wins + custom save_as; store:true‚Üístored_file_id/file-store url, store:false‚Üítelegram url no-write, runs-once-per-run merges on every item; failures no-tg / no-getFile / no-file_id / store-without-files / download-transport-error); node-harness gained a `getFile` recorder (+`getFileResult`/`getFileError`/`noGetFile`) + `files.write` (records `storedFiles`); registry-count tests bumped 33‚Üí34 (6 files). **verify GREEN:** typecheck clean (6 pkgs) + shared 63 / sandbox 49 / nodes 17(267) / core 16 / server 35(279) / editor 14(135).
Task-prevA: P6-T1 = PA-T1 `tg.sendMedia` ‚Äî Telegram media SEND (bytes + albums) ‚Äî DONE. A sibling of `tg.sendMessage` focused on rich media: send photo/video/document/audio from a `url`, a Telegram `file_id`, an UPLOADED Collection file (bytes), or `base64` ‚Äî and group 2‚Äì10 photo/video items into ONE album (media group). The node never touches disk or the Bot API directly: bytes come from a NEW nullable `ctx.files` capability (host reads the file-store) or are decoded from base64 in the node, and the actual upload is a NEW nullable `ctx.tg.sendMedia` host capability (`TgSender.sendMedia` maps to sendPhoto/Video/Document/Audio or sendMediaGroup, uploading bytes via grammY `InputFile`). Caption + parse-mode + keyboard preserved (album rule: photo/video only, no keyboard ‚Äî schema `superRefine`). Result passes input through adding `sent_message_ids: number[]` + `sent_message_id` (first). Fails LOUDLY when `ctx.tg.sendMedia` is absent, or when a `source:file` item has no `ctx.files` (I6). Task-prev0a: P5-T4 `ai.agent` ‚Äî tool loop (tools = MCP tools + flows-as-tools), step/cost budget caps ‚Äî DONE. An LLM that CALLS TOOLS in a multi-turn loop: the model decides which tool(s) to run with what JSON args, the node runs each + feeds the result back, looping until the model gives a final text answer OR a budget cap stops it. **Tools come from two GENERIC sources (I2):** `mcp` ‚Äî every tool an `mcpServer` credential's MCP server advertises (resolved at run start via `ctx.mcp.listTools`, each call goes through `ctx.mcp.callTool`); `subflow` ‚Äî another flow OF THE SAME BOT exposed as ONE named tool (n8n "Workflow Tool"; the model's JSON args become the sub-flow's entry `$json`, `flow.return` items become the tool result, runs through `ctx.subflow` so the same-bot + recursion-depth guards apply). The PROVIDER call is HOST-side via the EXTENDED `ctx.ai.chat()` (now carries `tools` + returns `toolCalls`) ‚Äî the node only ever passes a `credentialId`; keys never reach node code (I6/I7). **Budget caps (mandatory rails on an autonomous loop):** `max_steps` (assistant‚Üîtool round-trips, default 6), `max_tool_calls` (total invocations, default 12; **0 = tools advertised but forbidden** ‚Üí each requested call gets an `error:` string back), `max_tokens_total` (cumulative reported usage, 0 = no cap). On any cap the loop stops and returns the best answer so far with a `stopReason` ('final'|'max_steps'|'max_tool_calls'|'max_tokens'). Tool FAILURES (unknown tool, bad-JSON args, MCP `isError`, thrown runner) become an `error: ‚Ä¶` STRING fed back to the model ‚Äî NOT a node failure (an agent should recover by trying differently). Runs ONCE per node run; result `{reply, steps, toolCalls, usage, stopReason}` merges under `save_as` (default `agent`) onto every item (seeds one empty item if input empty); binary preserved; fails loudly when `ctx.ai` null, or when a configured `mcp`/`subflow` tool's capability is missing. Shared (I5): extended `AiChatMessage` (+`toolCalls?`/`toolCallId?`, role +`'tool'`), `AiChatRequest` (+`tools?`), `AiChatResult` (+`toolCalls?`), NEW `AiToolSpec`/`AiToolCall`; NEW `AiAgentParamsSchema`+`AgentToolSourceSchema`+`AgentToolSourceTypeSchema` (mcp needs `credentialId`; subflow needs `flow_id`; `tool_name` must be a valid function-name; superRefine). Server (`wire.ts`): `makeAi` now maps `req.tools`‚ÜíOpenAI `tools:[{type:'function',function:{name,description?,parameters}}]` + `toWireMessage()` translates assistant `toolCalls`‚Üí`tool_calls:[{id,type:'function',function:{name,arguments}}]` and tool results‚Üí`{role:'tool',tool_call_id,content}`; `parseChatCompletion()` extracts `message.tool_calls`‚Üí`AiToolCall[]` (id fallback `call_N`, args coerced to string). Editor: node auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n (parity compile-enforced; namespaced `paramDesc.ai.agent.{tools,max_steps,max_tool_calls,max_tokens_total}` + `option.ai.agent.type.{mcp,subflow}`). Registry **32** types. **Tests (+29):** nodes `ai-agent.test.ts` (25 ‚Äî registry-32, param schema defaults + mcp-needs-cred + subflow-needs-flow + malformed-tool_name, parseToolArguments, no-tools plain chat, MCP tool loop exposes/runs/feeds-back + isError‚Üíerror-message + unknown-tool‚Üíerror-not-failure, subflow-as-tool runs-with-$json + derives-name, budget caps max_steps/max_tool_calls/max_tokens_total/max_tool_calls=0, failure modes no-ai/no-mcp/no-subflow/chat-rejects) + server `ai-agent.test.ts` (4 ‚Äî e2e through the wired engine w/ fake routing fetch: MCP tool loop lists tools + passes function specs + calls tool w/ model args + feeds result back in wire shape + answers + both secrets stay host-side, plain-chat no-tools path, non-2xx fails the run, MCP tool `isError` surfaces as `error:` string to the model not a node failure). Registry-count tests bumped 31‚Üí32 (5 files). **verify GREEN:** shared 63 / sandbox 49 / nodes 15(240) / core 16 / server 35(279) / editor 14(135).
Task-prev0: P5-T3 `ai.mcpClient` + `mcpServer` credential DONE ‚Äî list/call tools on a Model-Context-Protocol server. The author picks an `mcpServer` credential (endpoint `url` + optional `apiKey`, encrypted at rest I7) and an action: **list_tools** ‚Üí `{tools}` (each `{name, description?, inputSchema?}`) or **call_tool** (`tool_name` + a JSON `arguments_json` object) ‚Üí `{result}` (`{content, text, isError}`). The MCP JSON-RPC call happens HOST-side via a NEW `ctx.mcp` capability (`listTools`/`callTool`) ‚Äî the node only ever passes a `credentialId`; the decrypted key NEVER reaches node code (invariants I6/I7). Runs ONCE per node run (a single tool call); the chosen value is merged under `save_as` (default `mcp`) onto every item (seeds one empty item if input is empty); binary preserved; fails loudly when `ctx.mcp` is null. `arguments_json` is parsed leniently (blank‚Üí`{}`, must be a JSON OBJECT ‚Äî array/primitive rejected); `call_tool` requires a non-blank `tool_name` (schema superRefine). Task-prev : P5-T1 `ai.llmChat` + `openAiApi` credential DONE ‚Äî the first AI node. An OpenAI-compatible LLM Chat node: the user picks an `openAiApi` credential (base_url + key, encrypted at rest I7) and a model; the node sends `system_prompt` + (optional) rolling conversation memory + `user_prompt` to `POST {baseUrl}/chat/completions` and merges `{reply, usage, model}` onto every output item under `save_as` (default `ai`). The PROVIDER call happens HOST-side via a NEW `ctx.ai.chat()` capability ‚Äî the node only ever passes a `credentialId` + model + messages; the decrypted key NEVER reaches node code (invariants I6/I7). Works with OpenAI / OpenRouter / Anthropic-proxy / any local OpenAI-compatible server (only base_url + key vary). **memory=conversation:** the last N turns (user+assistant) are persisted per-CHAT in KV (scope=user, key `__ai_mem__:<nodeId>` so two LLM nodes keep separate memories), loaded into the prompt + window-trimmed before/after each call; **memory=none** touches no KV. Runs ONCE per node run (not per item ‚Äî an LLM call is expensive + memory is per-chat). Shared (I5): `OpenAiApiSchema` added to `CredentialDataSchema` discriminatedUnion (+enum/labels/hint/authHeaders kept exhaustive), `AiLlmChatParamsSchema`+`AiMemorySchema`, `NodeCtx.ai` capability + `AiChatMessage/Request/Usage/Result` types. Task-prev2: P4-T4 Outgoing instance webhooks DONE. The open protocol's OUTBOUND edge ‚Äî CTB POSTs an event envelope when something happens. NEW `instance_webhooks` table (migration `0003_giant_nebula.sql`, 14 tables). Host-side `WebhookDispatcher` fans out the JSON envelope to every ACTIVE+subscribed+bot-scope-matching subscription (fire-and-forget w/ inflight-set `drain()`), optional `X-CTB-Signature` HMAC, 3x retry on transport/5xx/408/429 (not 4xx), stamps `last_fired_at`+`last_error`. Roadmap   : docs/PLAN.md (active, through Phase 6) ‚Üí then docs/PLAN2.md (n8n-parity: media + data-transform library + DB connectors + AI Agent w/ sub-nodes + speech + API/MCP builder surface). PLAN2 is a design doc until PLAN.md is done.
```

> ‚ÑπÔ∏è **Session note (P5-T4):** credits ran out once mid-task (during a `sed`
> fixing two assertion idioms in `ai-agent.test.ts` ‚Äî `res.items.main` should be
> `res.outputs.main`, and a `fail()` returns `{kind:'error'}` not `{kind:'fail'}`).
> On resume `git status` + a grep showed the `sed` had NOT landed, so it was
> re-run and the 25 node tests went green. The design choice worth recording:
> rather than invent a parallel tool-calling capability, P5-T4 EXTENDS the
> existing `ctx.ai.chat()` (adds `tools` in / `toolCalls` out) so a tool-using
> agent and a plain `ai.llmChat` share ONE host LLM path ‚Äî the OpenAI wire
> translation (`tool_calls`/`tool_call_id`) lives only in `wire.ts`. Tool errors
> are fed back to the model as `error:` strings (never node failures) so the
> agent can recover, matching n8n; only misconfiguration fails the node loudly.
> `npm run verify` green (server 279 / editor 135).
>
> ‚ÑπÔ∏è **Session note (P6-T1 = PA-T1):** the session was interrupted mid-task and
> resumed at the i18n step; on resume `git status` confirmed all code/test files
> had landed and `npm run typecheck` was clean, so the i18n keys were added to
> BOTH `fa.ts` and `en.ts` (parity is compile-enforced ‚Äî a missing en key is a
> COMPILE error) and the editor typecheck stayed green. The design choice worth
> recording: `tg.sendMessage` already had `type`/`media` params but the HOST
> `sendMessage` path silently ignored them, so media never actually sent ‚Äî
> rather than fix that overloaded node, PA-T1 adds a DEDICATED `tg.sendMedia`
> node plus two NEW nullable capabilities (`ctx.tg.sendMedia` for the Bot-API
> upload, `ctx.files` for reading stored bytes) so the node stays driver-free
> (I3) and fails loud when a capability is absent (I6). `npm run verify` green
> (shared 63 / sandbox 49 / nodes 16¬∑255 / core 16 / server 35¬∑279 / editor 14¬∑135).
>
> ‚ÑπÔ∏è **Session note (P5-T1):** the session dropped twice (once mid-edit of an
> en.ts i18n comma fix, once mid-edit of the `credentialRef` widget type filter);
> on each resume the workspace was intact and `git status` / a quick `grep`
> showed exactly which edits had landed, so work continued from there. The
> design choice worth recording: rather than overload the existing
> `credentials.authHeaders` capability (which only carries headers, not a
> base_url), P5-T1 introduces a dedicated `openAiApi` credential (base_url + key)
> + a dedicated `ctx.ai.chat()` capability ‚Äî the HOST performs the LLM call so
> the key never reaches node code (I6/I7), and every OpenAI-compatible provider
> (OpenAI/OpenRouter/Anthropic-proxy/local) is reached by varying only base_url +
> key. `npm run verify` green (server 269 / editor 135).

> webhook route so the documented recipe is real, not aspirational. `npm run

## Repo health ‚Äî verification commands

Run these to confirm the repo is in the expected state before working:

```bash
git status                 # must be clean
git log --oneline -3       # last task IDs should match the session log below
npm install && npm run verify          # ‚Üí must be green
CTB_SECRET=devsecret0123456 CTB_DB_PATH=/tmp/ctb.sqlite npm run db:migrate
# ‚Üí prints 12 tables: bots, collections, credentials, exec_logs, executions,
#   files, flow_versions, flows, kv_store, pending_triggers, records, users
# Boot smoke (Phase 0 demo):
CTB_SECRET=devsecret0123456 CTB_ADMIN_PASS=hunter2hunter2 CTB_DB_PATH=/tmp/ctb.sqlite npm run dev:server
curl localhost:3000/healthz                       # ‚Üí {"ok":true}
curl -X POST localhost:3000/api/auth/login -H 'content-type: application/json' \
  -d '{"username":"admin","password":"hunter2hunter2"}' -c /tmp/c.txt   # ‚Üí {"ok":true,...}
curl localhost:3000/api/auth/me -b /tmp/c.txt     # ‚Üí {"user":{"username":"admin"}}
```

Expected right now: **Phases 0‚Äì2 complete + P3-T1‚Ä¶P3-T5 done** (Phase 3 in
progress ‚Äî sub-flows, loop/merge, the four tg.* message ops, the encrypted

paragraphs below trace the build up through Phase 2; per-task detail for Phase 3
lives in the **session log** and the **What exists** table (rows P3-T1‚Ä¶P3-T5).
Next task is **P3-T6** (execution policies + per-flow error-handler flow). The flow editor
has canvas (P2-T2) **plus the schema-driven param side-panel (P2-T3)**:
select one node ‚Üí `ParamPanel` renders a form generated from the node's
`paramsJsonSchema` by a standalone form engine (`src/form/`: schema resolver
keyed by STRUCTURAL field shape, never node type ‚Äî Phase 3.5 Collections
reuse it as required by PLAN's architecture note). Widgets: expression-aware
text/multiline (accent border + {x} badge when a {{ }} expression is present,
$scope hints dropdown rendered position:fixed so the panel never clips it),
number,
boolean, select, duration (qty+unit ‚Üí "15m"), nested object, repeating rows,
union tabs (waitForReply prompt string|object), Telegram keyboard grid
builder (inline/reply/remove, structural detect), IF condition rows
(value1/operator/value2, structural detect). Draft params debounce-commit
(pruneEmpty) into the canvas store ‚Üí one undo step per edit ‚Üí existing
autosave PATCH pipeline. Node-level enable/disable + note controls included.
Panel polished n8n-style: every node + field carries a fa/en description
(`nodeDesc.*`/`paramDesc.*`), inputs have placeholders (`ph.*`), enum options
are translated (`option.*`); union tabs are a segmented control whose chosen
branch is LOCAL state (no snap-back when pruneEmpty empties the draft) and
branch switches carry the user's text via `convertBranchValue`.
**P2-T3.5 (n8n-style NDV):** double-click a node ‚Üí modal INPUT pane |
params | OUTPUT pane fed by the latest execution (executor records capped
per-step I/O into exec_logs ‚Üí `GET /api/executions[/:id]` ‚Üí run-data store);
schema/table/JSON views, per-port tabs; drag a field row onto any expression
input ‚Üí `{{ $json.path }}` inserted at the caret; per-node "n items" run
badge on canvas. Acceptance verified as headless tests (every P1 node
configured purely via widget operations ‚Üí params validate against the REAL
shared Zod schemas; fake server now serves z.toJSONSchema of the genuine
schemas) and live (PATCH panel-produced params ‚Üí server-validated ‚Üí read
back identical; SPA boots clean).
**P2-T4 (flow lifecycle):** activation now validates EVERY enabled node's
params via the shared pure `validateFlowForActivation` (`shared/src/
flow-validate.ts`; expression `{{ }}` values are never judged statically) ‚Üí
422 carries `problems: string[]` + structured `nodeProblems: FlowProblem[]`;
`GET /api/flows/:id/versions` (counts-only DTO) + `POST /:id/rollback`
(snapshot re-validated, outgoing graph snapshotted ‚Üí rollback is undoable);
editor: `stores/lifecycle.ts` (activate/deactivate/problems-by-node/version
list/rollback), toolbar status badge + activate/deactivate + ŸÜÿ≥ÿÆŸá‚ÄåŸáÿß dropdown
(restore ‚Üí saveNow first ‚Üí rollback ‚Üí canvas reload), problems strip under
the toolbar, ‚öÝ badge on offending canvas nodes.
**P2-T5 (executions inspector):** `POST /api/executions/:id/cancel`
(single guarded UPDATE waiting|running‚Üícanceled + wait cleared, mirrors the
router's /cancel; 409 `not_cancelable` on finished rows, audit exec_logs
row); `ApiClient.cancelExecution`; editor `stores/executions.ts` (list w/
status filter + flowId scope, detail selection, `refresh()` that re-syncs
list AND open detail with overlap guard ‚Äî the PAGE owns the 4s interval so
unmount can't leak, ticks skip when the tab is hidden, cancel applies the
server response then re-fetches the detail; 409/404 on cancel = silent
refresh, not an error); `ExecutionsPage` master-detail UI: status filter

node/retries/deadline) + cancel button (live runs only, confirm) + node-by-
node step log where "executed" rows expand into the SAME DataPanel panes
the NDV uses (schema/table/JSON, per-port tabs). `?flowId=` deep-link scope.
**P2-T6 (MVP nodes wave 2):** six new built-ins ‚Äî `tg.menu` (inline-button
grid ‚Üí one "btn:<key>" port per button + optional `timeout`; pauses with a
callback WaitSpec carrying per-key label/value meta + `answerText`; router
answers the callbackQuery and enriches `$json.clicked`; `edit_in_place`
edits the clicked menu message via the new optional `ctx.tg.editMessageText`
capability, falling back to a fresh send), `flow.switch` (first-matching-rule
routing, ports = rules + `default`), `flow.wait` (durable delay WaitSpec ‚Äî
duration or until-datetime, resumes via the scanner on `main`),
`http.request` (per-item via host-limited ctx.http; query/header/form rows,
JSON auto-spread into $json, `never_error`), `data.kv` (get/set/delete/
increment over ctx.kv, once per node run), `flow.manualTrigger` (sample-JSON
test entry; counts as a trigger for activation). IF's comparison semantics
extracted to `nodes/lib/compare.ts` (shared with switch). Dynamic ports:
`NodeDef.dynamicOutputs` on menu/switch + the shared `dynamicOutputPorts`
helper (draft-tolerant) in `shared/node-params.ts` ‚Äî canvas `effectiveOutputs`
renders one handle per button/rule and `canConnect` validates against the
params-derived list, so menu ports render as separate edges (acceptance).

A flow's DESIGN is portable via a versioned, identity-free JSON envelope. | Outgoing instance webhooks (P4-T4) | ‚úÖ DONE. PLAN P4-T4 + PROTOCOL.md ¬ßOutbound. The open protocol's **outbound edge** ‚Äî CTB POSTs an event envelope to subscribed URLs. NEW `instance_webhooks` table (id/name/url/secret/events(json)/bot_id‚Üíbots(cascade)/active/created_at/last_fired_at/last_error); migration `0003` (14 tables). NEW host-side `WebhookDispatcher` (`apps/server/src/engine/webhook-dispatcher.ts`): `dispatch(event)` loads every ACTIVE subscription matching the event name + bot scope (null=all bots), POSTs the JSON envelope (fire-and-forget; `await drain()` for tests/shutdown), optional `X-CTB-Signature: sha256=HMAC-SHA256(body,secret)`, retries ‚â§3x w/ linear backoff on transport err / 5xx / 408 / 429 (NOT 4xx), stamps `last_fired_at`+`last_error`. Three events: **execution.finished**/**execution.failed** from `SqliteExecutionStore.save()` terminal transition (new `setFinishedListener`); **user.first_seen** from `SqliteUserStore.touch()` insert path (new `setFirstSeenListener`) ‚Äî both best-effort, a throwing listener never breaks the write. `wire.ts` owns the dispatcher (always on `Engine`), attaches both listeners, passes `opts.fetchImpl` (tests inject fake fetch). Admin CRUD `api/instance-webhooks.ts` at `/api/instance-webhooks` (GET/POST/PATCH/DELETE; `400 unknown_bot`; PATCH 404). `secret` WRITE-ONLY ‚Äî never returned, public projection exposes only `hasSecret` (I7). | `data.editFields` node ‚Äî Edit Fields (Set) power node (PA-T3) | ‚úÖ DONE. PLAN2 PA-T3 + NODES.md ¬ßEdit Fields (Set). A richer sibling of `data.setFields` (kept UNTOUCHED for backward-compat ‚Äî this is a NEW node, NOT a relabel), labelled **"Edit Fields (Set)"** in the palette so n8n users find it. Same immutable per-item model (input items never mutated; `$vars` rows apply once per run; empty input still emits one shaped item) plus three powers per row over basic Set: (1) **op `rename`** ‚Äî move a value from one dotted path (`name`) to another (`value` = destination path), deleting the source; works in `keep_only_set` mode too (source read from the original item); (2) **`value_mode:'json'`** ‚Äî a STRING `value` is `JSON.parse`d into a real value/array/object (a non-string passes through unchanged); (3) **`enabled`** (default true) ‚Äî a disabled row stays in config but is skipped. Dotted names build nested objects; `keep_only_set` makes the output `$json` start empty. Fails LOUDLY (validated UP FRONT in a `planRow` pass before any item is touched) on a `value_mode:'json'` value that isn't valid JSON, or a `rename` with an empty destination. ## Session log (append-only, newest first)

| 2026-06-17 | PB-T4 | **Chat-memory providers ‚Äî `ai.memoryKv` (default) + `ai.memoryPostgres`; Phase B's first concrete *provider* sub-nodes.** PB-T1 added the typed sub-connection *contract* (a consumer's `ai:memory` slot, a provider's `role:'provider'`/`provides`) but shipped no real provider ‚Äî these two are the first. They are the n8n "Chat Memory" nodes, kept strictly generic (I2 ‚Äî memory is a capability, never a domain concept): a flow author attaches one to an AI Agent's `ai:memory` slot (a dashed sub-connection) and the Agent gains a **rolling conversation memory**. The crucial design point: **a provider is never executed as a data step** ‚Äî the PB-T1 executor already skips `role:'provider'` nodes, so a provider's *params* ARE its entire contract. The consumer (the AI Agent, landing in **PB-T5**) reads the attached provider's resolved params, turns them into a `ChatMemoryConfig`, and drives a shared runtime. That runtime is the heart of this task: NEW `packages/shared/src/chat-memory.ts` exposes `loadChatHistory(cfg, {kv, db})` (replay the rolling last-N turns before a model call) and `appendChatTurn(cfg, {kv, db}, {user, assistant})` (persist the new pair after), plus `kvMemoryKey()`, `quotePgIdent()` and `toAiMessages()`. It touches the world ONLY through the injected `ctx.kv`/`ctx.db` capabilities (I3/I6 ‚Äî it imports no database driver and never sees a decrypted secret; the host resolves `credentialId`‚Üípool), and it is the SAME logic `ai.llmChat`'s `memory:'conversation'` already used, now generalized. **Two backings, one contract:** `ai.memoryKv` (the DEFAULT) persists the trimmed window as a single JSON value in KV (`scope:'user'`, key `__ai_mem__:<session>`), so a bot with **no database** still remembers ‚Äî params `session_key` (blank ‚Üí keyed per node+chat) + `memory_window` (turns, default 10). `ai.memoryPostgres` persists turns as rows via `ctx.db`: `loadChatHistory` issues a `SELECT role, content FROM (‚Ä¶ ORDER BY id DESC LIMIT $2) ORDER BY id ASC` (newest window, replayed oldest-first), `appendChatTurn` writes the pair as **two bound rows in one `INSERT ‚Ä¶ VALUES ($1,$2,$3),($1,$4,$5)`** ‚Äî params `credentialId` (a `postgres` credential), `table` (default `ctb_chat_memory`, validated as a SQL identifier), `session_key`, `memory_window`, `auto_create` (issues `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` before first use). **SQL-injection safety carried over from PB-T2:** every value is a bound `$N` parameter (a test fires `'; DROP TABLE users; --` as the user message and asserts it stays a single param, never in the SQL text); the only interpolated text is the table identifier, validated per dot-segment against `/^[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*$/` and double-quoted by `quotePgIdent` (a hostile or backtick-bearing table throws loudly). Both paths fail LOUDLY when the needed capability is absent (`ctx.kv` for kv, `ctx.db` for postgres). **Shared (I5):** `chat-memory.ts` (runtime + `ChatMemoryConfig` discriminated union + `ChatMemoryMessage`) exported from the index; `AiMemoryKvParamsSchema`/`AiMemoryPostgresParamsSchema` + `ChatMemoryWindowSchema` in `node-params.ts`. **Nodes:** `ai/memory-kv.ts` + `ai/memory-postgres.ts` ‚Äî both `role:'provider'`, `provides:'ai:memory'`, `ports {inputs:[], outputs:['provider']}`, with an `execute()` that fails loud (defensive ‚Äî providers are config, never run) ‚Äî registered in `index.ts`. **Editor:** fa/en i18n in parity (compile-enforced; `i18n-namespace.test.ts`): `nodes.ai.memory{Kv,Postgres}.label` + `nodeDesc.ai.memory{Kv,Postgres}` + the full `param.ai.memory{Kv,Postgres}.*`/`paramDesc.*` families; the `credentialRef` widget already filters `ai.memoryPostgres` to `postgres` credentials, so no widget change. NODES.md ¬ßAI gained a "Chat memory providers (PB-T4)" subsection. **Gotcha (carried from PB-T1):** `NodeTypeSchema` is EXACTLY two dot-parts (`/^[a-z][a-zA-Z0-9]*\.[a-z][a-zA-Z0-9]*$/`), so the *registered* types are `ai.memoryKv`/`ai.memoryPostgres` (camelCase second segment, like `ai.llmChat`) even though the docs/PLAN refer to them conceptually as `ai.memory.kv`/`ai.memory.postgres`. Registry **44‚Üí46** types; all 13 nodes-registry-count guards bumped 44‚Üí46. **Server back-compat fix:** `node-types.test.ts`'s "omits role/inputSlots/provides for plain data nodes" guard (written when EVERY builtin was `role:'data'`) now skips the two memory providers, and a NEW sibling test asserts they DO surface `role:'provider'` + `provides:'ai:memory'` + `inputs:[]`/`outputs:['provider']` over the wire ‚Äî confirming PB-T1's conditional `node-types.ts` emission works for a real provider, not just a synthetic test fixture. **Tests (+18):** nodes `ai-memory.test.ts` (17 ‚Äî registry-46; both register as `ai:memory` providers with no data input; provider `execute` fails loud; param defaults + hostile-table rejection in the schema; KV runtime: fresh‚Üíempty, append+replay newest-last + stored under the namespaced key, window√ó2 trim drops the oldest turn, corrupt stored value ignored not thrown, KV-absent throws; Postgres runtime: auto-create THEN windowed `SELECT` bound by `$1/$2` (=`[session, window*2]`), rows mapped oldest-first with `autoCreate:false` skipping the CREATE, append as two bound rows with the hostile value staying a single param + no `DROP TABLE` in the SQL, `quotePgIdent('app.turns')='"app"."turns"'` + rejects `x; DROP TABLE y`, db-absent throws, `toAiMessages` shape) + server `node-types.test.ts` (+1). **`npm run verify` GREEN** (run per-workspace; full script times out at 120s in this sandbox ‚Äî typecheck all 6 workspaces clean; shared 73 / core 50 / sandbox 16 / nodes 447 / server 293 / editor 143 incl. i18n parity). Next: PB-T5 (`ai.agent` orchestrator ‚Äî consume the `ai:model`/`ai:memory`/`ai:tool` slots, wiring the memory providers shipped here into the agent loop). |
| 2026-06-17 | PB-T3 | **`db.mysql` ‚Äî a generic MySQL / MariaDB database node; Phase B's second DB connector.** The exact mirror of PB-T2's `db.postgres`, so a flow author who learned the Postgres node already knows this one ‚Äî it shares the SAME injected `ctx.db` capability, the same `query`/`select`/`insert`/`update`/`delete` operations, the same `return_mode`/`confirm_many`/`save_as` semantics, the same "values are ALWAYS bound, never concatenated" injection-safety rule, and the same "runs ONCE per node run, fails LOUDLY when `ctx.db` is null" contract. Kept strictly generic (I2 ‚Äî "MySQL" is infrastructure, never a domain concept) and the `mysql2` driver + connection POOL live ONLY in `apps/server` (I3 ‚Äî `core`/`nodes` import no DB driver). The connection comes from a NEW `mysql` credential (host/port[default 3306]/database/user/password/ssl) encrypted at rest (I7); the node only carries a `credentialId`. **Three real dialect differences from Postgres, each handled deliberately:** (1) placeholders are positional `?` rather than numbered `$1,$2,‚Ä¶` ‚Äî so `buildWhere` no longer threads an index, the values-array order *is* the placeholder order; (2) identifiers are **backtick**-quoted (`` `col` ``) not double-quoted, while the same strict `/^[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*$/` per-dot-segment validation guards against injection (a test fires a backtick-bearing AND a `; DROP TABLE` identifier and asserts both throw, while a hostile *value* stays a single bound `?` parameter); (3) MySQL has **no `RETURNING *`** ‚Äî a write returns the driver's OK packet, so the node emits no RETURNING and the host's `mysqlPoolFactory` normalizes the OK packet to a synthetic row `{affectedRows, insertId?}` so the `rows`/`single` return modes still behave like Postgres'. **Dialect routing:** `DbQueryRequest` gained an optional `dialect?: 'postgres'|'mysql'` (defaults `postgres`, so the PB-T2 node and its tests are byte-for-byte unchanged); the node sends `dialect:'mysql'`, and the host's `makeDb()` became dialect-aware (now a 4-arg `makeDb(db, key, pgFactory, mysqlFactory)`) ‚Äî `resolvePool(credentialId, dialect)` decrypts the credential, THROWS if `data.type !== dialect` (so a flow can't aim a Postgres node at a MySQL credential or vice-versa ‚Äî "credential ‚Ä¶ is not a {MySQL|Postgres} credential"), picks the matching factory, and caches one pool per credentialId. `mysqlPoolFactory` lazily `createRequire(import.meta.url)`-loads `mysql2` (apps/server is pure ESM ‚Äî a bare `require` is absent at runtime), wraps its callback pool via `.promise()`, and adapts `pool.query ‚Üí [rows|okPacket, fields]` to the `DbPool` contract (SELECT ‚Üí the row array; a write ‚Üí the normalized single row). It is INJECTABLE via `WireOptions.mysqlPoolFactory`, so the server e2e tests pass a recording fake (and assert the pg factory is NEVER called for a mysql credential) ‚Äî no real MySQL needed. **Shared (I5):** `MysqlSchema` added to the `CredentialDataSchema` discriminatedUnion (and `CredentialTypeSchema` enum / `CREDENTIAL_TYPE_LABELS` / `credentialHint()` / `credentialAuthHeaders()` all kept exhaustive ‚Äî each was a TS compile error until handled); `DbMysqlParamsSchema`/`DbMysqlParams` mirror `DbPostgres` but stamp `credentialType:'mysql'` on the `credentialRef` widget and reuse the shared `DbOperationSchema`/`DbWhereRowSchema`/`DbValueRowSchema`. **Nodes:** `packages/nodes/src/db/mysql.ts` + registered in `index.ts`. **Server:** `mysql2 ^3.15.4` runtime dep (3.22.5 installed) ‚Äî justified per CLAUDE.md ¬ß6: a generic MySQL node cannot speak the wire protocol without the official driver, and `mysql2` ships its own TypeScript types so no `@types` is needed. **Editor:** `CredentialsPage` gained a `mysql` credential form (host/port/database/user/password/ssl, blank fields omitted); the `credentialRef` widget already filters options by the param's `credentialType` meta, so the node automatically offers ONLY `mysql` credentials with no widget change; fa/en i18n added in parity (compile-enforced; `i18n-namespace.test.ts` asserts fa/en carry the same namespaced override-key set): `credentials.type.mysql` + `credentials.field.my{Host,Port,Database,User,Password,Ssl}` + `nodes.db.mysql.label` + `nodeDesc.db.mysql` + the full `param.db.mysql.*` / `paramDesc.db.mysql.*` families + `option.db.mysql.{operation,order_dir,return_mode}.*`. | 2026-06-17 | PB-T2 | **`db.postgres` ‚Äî a generic Postgres database node; Phase B's first DB connector.** n8n has a "Postgres" node; CTB needs the same, kept strictly generic (I2 ‚Äî "Postgres" is infrastructure, never a domain concept). The node speaks SQL through a NEW injected `ctx.db` capability and the actual `pg` driver + connection POOL live ONLY in `apps/server` ‚Äî `core` and `nodes` never import a database driver (I3, the same host-injects-capability pattern as `ctx.ai`/`ctx.mcp`/`ctx.files`). The connection comes from a NEW `postgres` credential (host/port/database/user/password/ssl) encrypted at rest (I7); the node only ever carries a `credentialId` and the host resolves it to a decrypted secret + a pooled connection ‚Äî the password never reaches node code or the flow JSON. **SQL-injection safety is the heart of the node:** values are ALWAYS bound as `$1,$2,‚Ä¶` parameters and never string-concatenated into the SQL; the `query` operation passes the author's SQL + a parsed params array straight through, while the `select`/`insert`/`update`/`delete` helpers BUILD the statement ‚Äî table/column identifiers are validated against `/^[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*$/` (per dot-segment) and double-quoted by `quoteIdent` (a hostile identifier throws loudly), and every WHERE/SET/VALUES value is threaded through `buildWhere`/`buildStatement` as a bound placeholder. A test fires a hostile value (`'; DROP TABLE ‚Ä¶`) and asserts it stays a single bound parameter, never reaching the SQL text. `return_mode` chooses rows (one output item per result row) or single (`{rows,rowCount}` merged under `save_as`); `confirm_many` is a guard rail on a multi-row UPDATE/DELETE (a single-equality WHERE is allowed without it, a broad one is refused unless `confirm_many` is set). The node runs ONCE per node run (a query shouldn't multiply by item count) and fails LOUDLY when `ctx.db` is null (host didn't inject it). **Shared (I5):** `PostgresSchema` added to the `CredentialDataSchema` discriminatedUnion (and the `CredentialTypeSchema` enum / `CREDENTIAL_TYPE_LABELS` / `credentialHint()` / `credentialAuthHeaders()` all kept exhaustive ‚Äî each was a TS compile error until handled), `NodeCtx.db` capability + `DbQueryRequest`/`DbQueryResult` types, and `DbWhereOpSchema`/`DbWhereRowSchema`/`DbValueRowSchema`/`DbOperationSchema`/`DbPostgresParamsSchema` in `node-params.ts`. **Core:** `ExecutorServices.db` (optional ‚Üí `ctx.db` null without it) + `buildCtx` wiring. **Server (`wire.ts`):** `makeDb(db, key, poolFactory)` owns a per-`credentialId` pool cache ‚Äî `resolvePool` decrypts the `postgres` credential, THROWS if the credential isn't `postgres`-typed (a misconfigured flow fails before any pool is built), and caches the pool so repeated runs reuse one connection pool; `closeAll()` drains every pool via `Promise.allSettled(end())`. The actual `pg.Pool` is built by `pgPoolFactory`, which lazily `createRequire(import.meta.url)`-loads `pg` (apps/server is `"type":"module"` with `module:ESNext`, so a bare `require` is absent at runtime ‚Äî `createRequire` is the sanctioned ESM‚ÜíCJS bridge). The factory is INJECTABLE via `WireOptions.dbPoolFactory`, so the server e2e tests supply a fake pool that records the connection config + every query + whether it was ended ‚Äî no real Postgres needed. `Engine.closeDbPools()` is exposed and `main.ts` calls it in graceful shutdown (after the sandbox pool). New runtime dep `pg ^8.21.0` (+ `@types/pg ^8.15.0` devDep) ‚Äî justified per CLAUDE.md ¬ß6: a generic Postgres node cannot speak the wire protocol without the official driver, and a hand-rolled protocol implementation would be both unsafe and far larger than the dependency. **Editor:** `CredentialsPage` gained a `postgres` credential form (host/port/database/user/password/ssl, blank fields omitted from the saved data); the `credentialRef` widget already filters its options by the param's `credentialType` meta, so the node automatically offers ONLY `postgres` credentials with no widget change; fa/en i18n added in parity (compile-enforced ‚Äî a missing en key is a COMPILE error, and `i18n-namespace.test.ts` asserts fa/en carry the same namespaced override-key set): `credentials.type.postgres` + `credentials.field.pg{Host,Port,Database,User,Password,Ssl}` + `nodes.db.postgres.label` + `nodeDesc.db.postgres` + the full `param.db.postgres.*` / `paramDesc.db.postgres.*` families + `option.db.postgres.{operation,order_dir,return_mode}.*`. NODES.md gained a "Database connectors" section (Postgres spec + a planned MySQL stub). That's why the demo AGGREGATES first then formats (by `compose`/`stamp` time there is a single item so `$json.titles[i]` resolves correctly), and uses `data.dateTime` `source:now` (reads `ctx.now()` directly, unaffected) for the headline Jalali stamp rather than a per-item `value`. Likewise `data.filter` is batch-level (conditions resolved once against item[0]; the same verdict routes the whole batch). | 2026-06-17 | PA-T7 | **`data.dateTime` ‚Äî Date & Time with IANA timezones AND the Jalali (Persian) calendar; the data-transform library's first calendar-aware node.** Mirrors n8n's "Date & Time" node but adds a first-class need for our Iranian users: formatting `€±€¥€∞€¥/€∞€≥/€≤€¥` (Persian digits, Jalali year). PURE ‚Äî the only clock is the injected `ctx.now()`, and the Gregorian‚ÜîJalali conversion is a small hand-written **dependency-free** algorithm in `packages/nodes/src/lib/jalali.ts` (Borkowski method, the one popularised by `jalaali-js`) rather than a new runtime dep (CLAUDE.md: "no new runtime dependency without justification"); I verified that hand-rolled algorithm against the platform's own `Intl` Persian calendar over **1,836 dates (2000‚Äì2050) with ZERO mismatches** before trusting it. Runs **per item**, merging the result under `save_as` (default `datetime`) onto a CLONE of each input item (never mutated; seeds one empty item if input is empty). Three operations: **`format`** ‚Üí `{ formatted, iso, epoch }` (the timezone-adjusted wall-clock rendered in the chosen calendar via a token pattern `YYYY/MM/DD/HH/mm/ss` + `MMMM` month-name, with `digits:'persian'` mapping `0-9`‚Üí`€∞-€π`); **`add`** ‚Üí `{ iso, epoch }` (shift by `amount`¬∑`unit`, negative subtracts; `years`/`months` use UTC calendar math, smaller units are exact millis); **`diff`** ‚Üí `{ diff, unit }` (`source ‚àí to_value` in `diff_unit`, may be fractional). The wall-clock is extracted via `Intl.DateTimeFormat(..).formatToParts` in the chosen IANA `timezone` (empty = UTC) ‚Äî so e.g. `2026-06-11T22:00Z` formatted in `Asia/Tehran` correctly rolls to the NEXT Jalali day `1405/03/22`. Lenient `parseDate` accepts epoch-millis, ISO-8601, and `YYYY-MM-DD` / `YYYY/MM/DD`; `source:'value'` runs the raw string through `ctx.eval` first so `{{ }}` expressions resolve. Shared (I5): `DataDateTimeParamsSchema` with a `superRefine` that requires `value` when `source=value`, `amount` when `operation=add`, and `to_value` when `operation=diff`, plus an identifier-only `save_as`; `amount` is `z.coerce.number()` so a widget string coerces. | 2026-06-17 | PA-T6 | **`data.sort` + `data.limit` + `data.removeDuplicates` ‚Äî small, pure, high-value item-list ops; the data-transform library continues.** Three n8n core "Sort / Limit / Remove Duplicates" siblings, all pure functions over the item list. **`data.sort`** does a STABLE multi-key sort ‚Äî the first `fields` row is the primary key, later rows break ties; values that are numbers or numeric strings compare numerically (so `'9' < '21' < '100'`, not lexically), everything else compares as a locale-aware string; a missing / null / empty value always sorts LAST regardless of asc/desc, and crucially that "missing last" rule is resolved BEFORE the `desc` negation (a na√Øve `-cmp` would have flipped empties to the top under descending ‚Äî a subtle bug avoided by handling missing explicitly in `compareKey`); the input array is never mutated (we sort a `.slice()`). **`data.limit`** keeps the first N (default) or last N items ‚Äî `max_items` is `z.coerce.number().int().min(0).default(10)` so a string from a widget coerces, `0` means no limit, and `‚â• length` passes everything through; same item references survive in their original relative order. **`data.removeDuplicates`** drops repeats keeping the FIRST occurrence (n8n's behaviour) with survivor order preserved; `compare:'all_fields'` (default) compares the WHOLE `$json` via a recursive key-SORTED stable serialization (so `{a:1,b:2}` and `{b:2,a:1}` dedupe), `compare:'selected_fields'` keys off the combined value at the chosen dotted `fields`, and a missing field is encoded as a distinct `\u0000undefined` sentinel so it never collides with a literal `null`; it `fail()`s loudly when `selected_fields` is chosen but no `fields` are supplied. Shared (I5): `SortFieldRowSchema` (field min-1 + order asc|desc default asc) + `DataSortParamsSchema` (fields min-1); `DataLimitParamsSchema` (max_items coerce/int/min0/default10 + keep first|last); `DataRemoveDuplicatesParamsSchema` (compare all_fields|selected_fields + fields string[] optional). Nodes `packages/nodes/src/data/{sort,limit,remove-duplicates}.ts` (registered, palette order after aggregate). Editor: all three auto-surface in the registry-driven palette; fa/en i18n keys added to BOTH catalogs (parity is compile-enforced, so a missing en key is a TS error) ‚Äî labels, `nodeDesc.*`, `paramDesc.*`, and translated enum options for order/keep/compare. NODES.md gained ¬ßSort + ¬ßLimit + ¬ßRemove Duplicates. Registry **38‚Üí41** types; all 9 registry-count guard tests bumped. **Tests (+27):** `data-sort-limit-dedupe.test.ts` ‚Äî sort (numeric-asc / numeric-string / desc / multi-key tie-break / locale-string / missing-last in BOTH directions / stable / no-mutate / empty / reject-empty-fields), limit (first / last / 0=no-limit / ‚â•length / coerce-string / empty / reject-negative), removeDuplicates (all-fields dedupe / key-order-irrelevant / selected-fields / multi-field key / missing‚âÝnull / order-preserved / empty / fail-when-no-fields). | 2026-06-17 | PA-T3 | **`data.editFields` ‚Äî the n8n "Edit Fields / Set" power node; the data-transform library begins.** PLAN2 Phase A pairs Telegram media completeness (PA-T1/PA-T2, now merged) with a generic data-transform node library mirroring n8n's core nodes; PA-T3 is its first member. We already had a basic `data.setFields`, but n8n's "Edit Fields (Set)" is a power node ‚Äî so rather than overload/relabel the existing node (which other flows may already reference), PA-T3 adds a NEW node `data.editFields`, labelled **"Edit Fields (Set)"** in the palette so n8n users find it, leaving `data.setFields` UNTOUCHED for backward-compat. It keeps the same safe, immutable per-item model as `data.setFields` ‚Äî input items are never mutated (each output is a fresh object via `structuredClone`), `target:'vars'` rows write `$vars` exactly ONCE per run (not per item), and an empty input still emits one shaped item ‚Äî then adds three powers per row: (1) **op `rename`** moves a value from one dotted path (the row's `name`) to another (the row's `value`, interpreted as a destination path) and deletes the source ‚Äî and it works in `keep_only_set` mode too, reading the source from the ORIGINAL item even though the output started empty; (2) **`value_mode:'json'`** treats a STRING `value` as JSON and `JSON.parse`s it into a real value / array / object (a non-string value passes straight through, so a pre-built object isn't double-encoded); (3) **`enabled`** (default true) lets a row stay in the saved config but be skipped on this run. Dotted `name`s build nested objects on set; `keep_only_set` makes the output `$json` start empty (only set/renamed fields survive). It fails LOUDLY ‚Äî but does so by validating EVERYTHING UP FRONT in a `planRow` pass (inside a try/catch that returns `fail()`) BEFORE any item is touched: a `value_mode:'json'` value that isn't valid JSON, or a `rename` with a blank destination path, aborts the whole node cleanly instead of throwing mid-item-map (the bug found+fixed this session ‚Äî `planRow` returns a pre-validated `PlannedRow {row, value, dest?}` that the per-item loop just applies). **Shared (I5):** `EditFieldRowSchema` (`name` min-1, `value` optional unknown, `target` json\|vars default json, `op` set\|remove\|rename default set, `value_mode` value\|json default value, `enabled` default true) + `DataEditFieldsParamsSchema` (`fields` min-1 + `keep_only_set` default false) + `EditFieldRow`/`DataEditFieldsParams` types; the existing `SetFieldRowSchema`/`DataSetFieldsParamsSchema` left exactly as-is. **Node:** NEW `packages/nodes/src/data/edit-fields.ts` (`dataEditFields: NodeDef`, type `data.editFields`, category `data`, pure helpers `planRow`/`getPath`/`setPath`/`removePath`); registered in `packages/nodes/src/index.ts` (import + export + `builtinNodes`). **Editor:** the node auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa (source-of-truth) + en (parity, `Record<keyof fa,string>`) gained `nodes.data.editFields.label` ("Edit Fields (Set)"), `nodeDesc.data.editFields`, `option.op.rename`, namespaced `paramDesc.data.editFields.{fields,value_mode,enabled,keep_only_set}`, and `option.editFields.value_mode.{value,json}`. NODES.md gained a ¬ßEdit Fields (Set) subsection. Registry **35** types. **Tests (+14):** NEW `packages/nodes/test/data-edit-fields.test.ts` (registry-35 assertion; set dotted+immutable / json-mode array+object / json-mode non-string passthrough; remove dotted; rename json + rename in keep_only_set + rename vars; keep_only_set drops the rest; disabled-row skipped; vars written once-per-run; empty-input seeds one item; failures empty-fields / blank-name ‚Üí `/invalid params/`, bad json value ‚Üí `/not valid JSON/i`, empty rename dest ‚Üí `/destination path is empty/i`). | 2026-06-17 | PA-T2 | **`tg.getFile` ‚Äî Telegram media RECEIVE (download + store); the symmetric sibling of PA-T1.** PA-T1 added media SEND (`tg.sendMedia`); PA-T2 completes the pair with media RECEIVE: given a Telegram `file_id` (captured by the trigger from a photo/voice/document/video the user sent), the node DOWNLOADS the bytes and OPTIONALLY STORES them so downstream nodes (`tg.sendMedia` `source:file`, the future `ai.speechToText`) can reuse them ‚Äî this is the "Get a file" left-half of the AI-voice screenshot needed for Phase B. The node touches neither the bot token, the network, nor disk (invariants I3/I6): a NEW nullable `ctx.tg.getFile(file_id)` host capability returns `{bytes, filePath, size, mime}` (the host calls the Bot-API `getFile` through the EXISTING rate-limited `TgSender.call` to learn the `file_path`/size, then `fetch`-downloads the raw bytes from `https://api.telegram.org/file/bot<token>/<file_path>` ‚Äî the token lives host-side in a NEW `BotHandle.token` field, never reaching node code), and when `store` is on the node hands the bytes to a NEW `ctx.files.write(bytes, mime)` capability (host `putLocal` writes them under the file-store, stamping the run's bot). `file_id` defaults to a `$json` lookup ‚Äî it tries `$json.file_id`, then the common nested shapes a trigger/normalizer emits (`reply`/`photo`/`voice`/`document`/`audio`/`video` `.file_id`) ‚Äî so the node drops in right after a media trigger with NO config; an explicit param (literal or `{{ }}`) always wins. It runs ONCE per node run (one download), merging a result object `{file_id, path, url, mime, size, stored_file_id?}` under `save_as` (default `file`) onto every input item (seeding one empty item if input is empty); `stored_file_id` + the file-store `url` appear only when `store` is on, otherwise `url` is the temporary Telegram download URL. Fails LOUDLY only on misconfiguration / honest errors: no `ctx.tg` or no `ctx.tg.getFile`, `store:true` with no `ctx.files` wired, no resolvable `file_id`, or a download/transport error. **Shared (I5):** `TgGetFileParamsSchema` (`file_id` default `''`, `store` default `true`, `save_as` identifier-regex default `'file'`, `.strict()`) + `TgGetFileParams`; a `TgStoredFile` interface (the public projection `ctx.files.write` returns ‚Äî the subset of `FilePublic` the node needs); an OPTIONAL `ctx.tg.getFile?(fileId)‚Üí{bytes,filePath,size,mime}`; and `ctx.files` extended from `{read}` to `{read, write}`. **Core:** `ExecutorServices.files` changed from a plain object to a **per-bot factory** `(botId)=>{read,write}` (the DL #15 pattern shared with `tg`/`users`/`collections`) ‚Äî `write` needs the run's bot to stamp ownership, while `read` ignores it (file ids are globally unique); `buildCtx` now calls `services.files(exec.botId)`. **Server:** `gateway.ts` adds a `token: string` to `BotHandle` (set in `registerBot`); `wire.ts` `makeFiles(fileStore, botId)` gains `write(bytes,mime)`‚Üí`fileStore.putLocal(botId, Buffer.from(bytes), mime)`‚Üímapped to `TgStoredFile`, `services.files` becomes `(botId)=>makeFiles(fileStore, botId)`, and the `ctx.tg` factory gains `getFile` (rate-limited `sender.call('getFile',{file_id})` ‚Üí build the file URL with `handle.token` ‚Üí `(opts.fetchImpl ?? fetch)(url)` ‚Üí bytes, with loud errors on a missing `file_path` or a non-ok response). **Editor:** the node auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa (source-of-truth) + en (parity, `Record<keyof fa,string>`) gained `nodes.tg.getFile.label`, `nodeDesc.tg.getFile`, and namespaced `paramDesc.tg.getFile.{file_id,store,save_as}`. NODES.md gained a ¬ßGet a File subsection. | 2026-06-15 | P5-T4 | **`ai.agent` ‚Äî the AI Agent tool loop (PLAN.md's final task; Phase 5 complete).** An LLM that CALLS TOOLS in a multi-turn loop: each round the model sees the conversation + the available tool specs and either (a) returns a final text answer ‚Üí the loop stops with `stopReason:'final'`, or (b) requests one-or-more tool calls ‚Üí the node runs each, appends the assistant's tool-call turn + each `role:'tool'` result back into the message list, and loops. **Two GENERIC tool sources (invariant I2 ‚Äî nothing domain-specific):** `mcp` = the author picks an `mcpServer` credential and the agent lists ALL its tools at run start (via `ctx.mcp.listTools`), exposing each as a callable tool (each invocation ‚Üí `ctx.mcp.callTool`); `subflow` = another flow OF THE SAME BOT exposed as ONE named tool (n8n's "Workflow Tool" ‚Äî the model's JSON arguments become the sub-flow's entry `$json={‚Ä¶args}`, the items its `flow.return` produced become the tool's text result, run through `ctx.subflow` so the existing same-bot + recursion-depth guards apply). The PROVIDER call is HOST-side via the EXTENDED `ctx.ai.chat()` capability (now carrying `tools` + returning `toolCalls`) ‚Äî the node only ever passes a `credentialId` + model + messages + tool specs; the decrypted key NEVER reaches node code (invariants I6/I7). **Budget caps are mandatory rails on an autonomous loop:** `max_steps` (assistant‚Üîtool round-trips, default 6 ‚Üí `stopReason:'max_steps'`), `max_tool_calls` (total invocations, default 12 ‚Üí `'max_tool_calls'`; **`0` = tools advertised but invocation forbidden**, so each requested call gets an `error: tool calls are disabled` string back ‚Äî the model still sees its tools but can't run them), `max_tokens_total` (cumulative reported usage checked after each LLM turn, `0`=no cap ‚Üí `'max_tokens'`). On any cap the loop returns the best answer so far + the `stopReason`. **Tool FAILURES become an `error: ‚Ä¶` STRING fed back to the model, never a node failure** (unknown tool name, non-JSON / non-object arguments, an MCP `isError` result, or a thrown runner) ‚Äî an agent should be able to recover by trying differently, exactly like n8n; a tool runner's throw is also `ctx.log('warn',‚Ä¶)`'d. The node fails LOUDLY only for misconfiguration (no `ctx.ai`; a configured `mcp` tool with no `ctx.mcp`; a configured `subflow` tool with no `ctx.subflow`) or a transport error from `ctx.ai.chat()`. Runs ONCE per node run (an agent loop is expensive external work + the conversation is singular); the result `{reply, steps, toolCalls, usage, stopReason}` merges under `save_as` (default `agent`) onto EVERY input item (seeds one empty `{json:{}}` when input is empty, like `ai.llmChat`/`ai.mcpClient`); binary preserved. **Shared (I5):** EXTENDED the tool-calling contract on the existing AI types ‚Äî `AiChatMessage` (role +`'tool'`, +`toolCalls?: AiToolCall[]`, +`toolCallId?`), `AiChatRequest` (+`tools?: AiToolSpec[]`), `AiChatResult` (+`toolCalls?: AiToolCall[]`); NEW `AiToolSpec {name, description?, parameters?}` + `AiToolCall {id, name, argumentsJson}`. NEW `AiAgentParamsSchema` (credentialRef‚Üí`openAiApi`, model, system/user prompts, `tools: AgentToolSource[]`, temperature?, max_tokens?, the three caps, save_as) + `AgentToolSourceSchema` (`type` mcp\|subflow, `credentialId`, `flow_id` w/ `flowRef` widget, `tool_name`, `description`; superRefine: mcp needs `credentialId`, subflow needs `flow_id`, a non-blank `tool_name` must be a valid JS function-name) + `AgentToolSourceTypeSchema`. **Server (`wire.ts`):** `makeAi` now maps `req.tools` ‚Üí OpenAI `tools:[{type:'function', function:{name, description?, parameters}}]`; NEW `toWireMessage()` translates an assistant turn's `toolCalls` ‚Üí `tool_calls:[{id, type:'function', function:{name, arguments: argumentsJson}}]` and a `role:'tool'` result ‚Üí `{tool_call_id, content}`; `parseChatCompletion()` extracts `message.tool_calls` ‚Üí `AiToolCall[]` (id fallback `call_<n>`, arguments coerced to a string; only sets `result.toolCalls` when non-empty). **Editor:** the node auto-surfaces in the registry-driven palette; fa/en label + nodeDesc + namespaced `paramDesc.ai.agent.{tools,max_steps,max_tool_calls,max_tokens_total}` (the shared model/prompt/temperature/max_tokens/save_as keys are reused) + `option.ai.agent.type.{mcp,subflow}` (parity compile-enforced ‚Äî en mirrors fa as `Record<keyof fa,string>`). Registry **32** types. **Tests (+29):** nodes `ai-agent.test.ts` (25 ‚Äî registry-32 + category/ports, param-schema defaults + mcp-needs-cred + subflow-needs-flow + malformed-tool_name, `parseToolArguments` blank/object/array-reject, no-tools plain-chat path, MCP loop exposes-tools/runs/feeds-result-back + `isError`‚Üíerror-string + unknown-tool‚Üíerror-not-failure, subflow-as-tool runs-with-model-args-as-$json + derives-name-from-flow-id, budget caps max_steps / max_tool_calls / max_tokens_total / max_tool_calls=0, failure modes no-ai / no-mcp / no-subflow / chat-rejects) + server `ai-agent.test.ts` (4 e2e through the WIRED engine w/ a URL-routing fake fetch: full MCP tool loop ‚Äî tools/list ‚Üí chat turn-1 tool_call ‚Üí tools/call w/ the model's args ‚Üí chat turn-2 final, asserting the function-spec passed to the provider, the assistant `tool_calls` + `role:'tool'` wire shapes on the replay, the merged result, AND both the openAiApi + mcpServer secrets staying host-side; plain-chat no-tools path; non-2xx fails the run; an MCP `isError` surfaces as an `error:` tool-result string to the model, not a node failure). | 2026-06-14 | P5-T2 | **`ai.classify` + `ai.extract` ‚Äî two more AI nodes, both over the EXISTING `ctx.ai.chat()` capability (no `wire.ts` change).** **`ai.classify`** is an LLM-powered Switch: the author lists `categories[]` (each a `key` + a `description`) and the node grows one DYNAMIC output port per category key PLUS a reserved `other` fallback; a single LLM call (a system message that lists the categories + a strict-classifier instruction, plus the user's `input`) routes the WHOLE batch to the chosen category's port. It runs ONCE per node run ‚Äî like `ai.llmChat`, routing a single conversation turn must not multiply cost by item count ‚Äî and the reply‚Üíkey match is deliberately tolerant: case-insensitive exact match first, then whole-token containment (so "This is spam." ‚Üí `spam`), else `other`; surrounding quotes/backticks/periods are stripped before matching. All ports are pre-seeded empty (so downstream `inputsByPort` is honest) and `{category}` is merged under `save_as` (default `classification`). **`ai.extract`** turns free text into a typed JSON object: the author lists `fields[]` (each `name` + `type` ‚àà string\|number\|boolean + `description` + `required`); the node sends a field-schema instruction, then on the reply strips ` ```json ` fences + any surrounding prose, `JSON.parse`s, requires an object, coerces each field per-type ("30"‚Üí30, "yes"/"true"/"1"‚Üítrue), DROPS unknown keys, fills missing OPTIONAL fields with `null`, and fails a missing REQUIRED field ‚Äî RETRYING up to `max_retries` (default 2 ‚Üí max+1 attempts) on bad-JSON / missing-required by appending the rejection reason as an extra system message to the retry prompt, before finally `fail()`ing; the validated object is merged under `save_as` (default `extracted`). A transport error from `ctx.ai.chat()` is NOT retried (it's not a model-output problem). Both nodes `fail()` loudly when `ctx.ai` is null. Shared (I5): NEW `AiClassifyParamsSchema` + `ClassifyCategorySchema` (`key` is PortName-safe + may not be the reserved `other`) + `classifyOutputs()`; NEW `AiExtractParamsSchema` + `ExtractFieldSchema` + `ExtractFieldTypeSchema`; the editor-side `dynamicOutputPorts(type)` mirror gained an `'ai.classify'` branch (draft-tolerant, identical port set to the engine's `dynamicOutputs` ‚Äî pinned by a cross-check test). Both nodes registered in `builtinNodes` (registry **28‚Üí30**). Editor: the nodes auto-appear in the registry-driven palette (category `ai`); fa/en labels + `nodeDesc.*` + `paramDesc.{input,categories}` + `paramDesc.ai.extract.{fields,max_retries}` + `option.type.{string,number,boolean}` (en parity compile-enforced). **üêõ i18n collision found & fixed:** `paramDesc.fields` and `paramDesc.max_retries` already exist (generic keys used by other nodes), so I used the NAMESPACED lookup the panel already supports (`paramDesc.<node.type>.<key>` falls back to bare `paramDesc.<key>` via `resolveNs`, namespace set to `node.type` in `ParamPanel`) ‚Üí `paramDesc.ai.extract.fields` / `paramDesc.ai.extract.max_retries`, sidestepping the TS1117 duplicate-key error without disturbing the existing generic keys. **Tests (+22):** NEW `packages/nodes/test/ai-classify-extract.test.ts` (registry-30, category/port shapes, classify dynamic-ports + shared‚Üîeditor mirror agreement, classify routing/messages/save_as/system_prompt, tolerant match case/punct/token, `other` fallback, runs-once, no-ai fail, chat()-reject; extract parse+coerce+drop-unknown+fence-strip+null-optional, retry-on-bad-json, retry-on-missing-required, fail-after-max+1, no-ai fail, transport-error no-retry). | 2026-06-14 | P4-T4 | **Outgoing instance webhooks ‚Äî the open protocol's outbound edge.** CTB now POSTs an event envelope to subscribed URLs when a run finishes/fails or a brand-new user is seen. NEW `instance_webhooks` table (`id/name/url/secret/events(json)/bot_id‚Üíbots(cascade)/active/created_at/last_fired_at/last_error`; migration `0003_giant_nebula.sql`, 14 tables). NEW host-side `WebhookDispatcher` (`apps/server/src/engine/webhook-dispatcher.ts`): `dispatch(event)` loads every ACTIVE subscription whose `events` include the event name AND whose bot scope matches (null = all bots, else the event's bot), then POSTs the JSON envelope `{event,bot_id,flow_id,execution_id,chat_id,at,data}` to each ‚Äî FIRE-AND-FORGET (tracked in an inflight set so tests + graceful shutdown can `await drain()`), so a slow/broken endpoint never blocks or fails the event source. Optional `X-CTB-Signature: sha256=HMAC-SHA256(rawBody, secret)` (reuses the inbound webhook trigger's header constant) when the subscription carries a secret. Delivery retries up to 3x with linear backoff on a transport error or a `5xx`/`408`/`429`, but NOT on a `4xx` (treated as a bad request); each attempt stamps `last_fired_at` + `last_error` (success clears the error). **Three events:** `execution.finished` (status‚Üídone) / `execution.failed` (status‚Üíerror) are emitted from `SqliteExecutionStore.save()` on the TERMINAL transition via a new `setFinishedListener`; `user.first_seen` is emitted from `SqliteUserStore.touch()` on the INSERT path via a new `setFirstSeenListener` ‚Äî both listeners are best-effort and guarded so a throwing/slow subscriber can never break the underlying DB write. `wire.ts` constructs the dispatcher (always present on `Engine`), wires both listeners (building the `OutboundEvent` envelopes with bot/flow/exec/chat ids + an `at` timestamp), and forwards `opts.fetchImpl` so tests inject a fake fetch. Admin-only management `api/instance-webhooks.ts` at `/api/instance-webhooks` (GET list / POST‚Üí201 `{webhook}` with `400 unknown_bot` for a bad scope / PATCH partial-update with 404 / DELETE) ‚Äî the `secret` (HMAC key) is WRITE-ONLY: accepted on create/update, NEVER returned; the public projection exposes only `hasSecret` (I7). Shared (I5): `OUTBOUND_EVENTS`, `OutboundEventName`, `OutboundEvent`, `CreateInstanceWebhookBody`, `UpdateInstanceWebhookBody`, `InstanceWebhookPublic` in `packages/shared/src/api.ts`; PROTOCOL.md ¬ßOutbound filled in with the implemented behavior (events table + subscription routes + delivery semantics). **Tests (+13):** server `instance-webhooks.test.ts` over real in-memory SQLite ‚Äî the dispatcher unit (fan-out to active+subscribed only, bot-scope filter, HMAC signature, retry-on-5xx then stamp `last_error`, recover-when-a-retry-succeeds clears the error, no-retry-on-4xx), the CRUD (auth required, secret never returned, empty-events + unknown-bot ‚Üí 400, PATCH toggle/edit + 404, DELETE), and the two real event sources (a finished execution fires `execution.finished`; touching a brand-new user fires `user.first_seen` EXACTLY ONCE); `db.test.ts` EXPECTED_TABLES gained `instance_webhooks`. **verify GREEN:** typecheck clean (6 pkgs) + shared 8 / core 6 / nodes 11(157) / sandbox 1 / server 31(264) / editor 14(135). **Session note:** several brief disconnects; on resume the workspace was intact, so finished by wiring the CRUD + running tests (two FK test-seed fixes: seed `bots` before bot-scoped webhooks; use a real flow id in the e2e execution test). (b) **Records store** NEW `apps/editor/src/stores/records.ts` ‚Äî Zustand factory `createRecordsStore(client)` + `useRecords` singleton; `query`/`createRecord`/`updateRecord`/`deleteRecord`. Key contract: a 422 from the server is NOT thrown ‚Äî `extractFieldErrors(err)` turns the `ApiError` body's `fields: FieldError[]` into a `FieldErrors = Record<dottedPath, message>` map that create/update RETURN, so the form can render validation inline keyed by field path (including `variants[0].stock`). (c) **Record form** NEW `pages/collections/RecordForm.tsx` ‚Äî renders one widget per `CollectionField` type (richer than the JSON-Schema form engine, permitted by PLAN's "extended with widgets"): scalar inputs, `select`‚Üí`<select>`, `multiSelect`‚Üí`MultiSelectWidget` chip-set, `boolean`‚Üícheckbox, `json`/`longText`‚Üí`textarea.mono`, **`image`/`file`‚Üí`FileWidget`** (FileReader‚Üíbase64‚Üí`api.uploadFile` ‚Üí stores the returned file id; image preview / file link / clear), **`relation`‚Üí`RelationWidget`** (`<select>` for kind=one, chip toggles for kind=many; options fetched via `api.queryRecords` over the target collection by slug, labelled by `recordTitle`), **`group`‚Üí`GroupWidget`** (repeating rows, each a recursive `FieldEditor` over the sub-fields, add/remove row, dotted-path errors). Submit: `existing ? updateRecord(id,{mode:'replace'}) : createRecord(...)`; a returned `FieldErrors` map renders inline and blocks navigation. `fileToBase64` strips the `data:` prefix.
